Jamison Brereton

32
Indra
Hiraс╣Зyast┼лpa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This justly famous hymn tells of IndraтАЩs most significant victory, his triumph over Vr╠еtra and the release of the waters, in perhaps the clearest treatment of this primal myth in the R╠еgveda. Vr╠еtra was a gigantic cobra who lay coiled around a mountain within which all the waters were entrapped. In his battle with Indra, Vr╠еtra spread his тАЬshoulders,тАЭ his cobraтАЩs hood, and struck at Indra with his fangs, but Indra finally killed Vr╠еtra with his mace, broke open the mountain, and let the waters pour out. They then flowed to Manu (vs. 8), who was the first sacrificer, and by implication to his descendants. Vr╠еtraтАЩs name means тАЬobstacle,тАЭ and this victory over тАЬObstacleтАЭ is therefore paradigmatic for IndraтАЩs victory over all obstacles.
Despite the relative clarity of the treatment of the Vr╠еtra battle, the hymn has a curious structure, obsessively circling around and alternately focusing in on and drawing back from the moment of dramatic confrontation between the adversar ies. After the initial verses of summary and the preliminaries to the battle (vss. 1тАУ4), the next three verses (5тАУ7) depict the battle, and it is portrayed as extremely one-sided, with the overconfident Vr╠еtra overmatched from the beginning and deci sively smashed by Indra. (The signature verb of the first section of the hymn is тИЪhan тАЬsmash, smite.тАЭ) Defeated and dismembered, Vr╠еtra lies there (the signature verb of this section is тИЪ┼Ы─л тАЬlieтАЭ) with his mother, and the released waters flow over them (8тАУ11). After this interlude the hymn returns to a new description of the battle (12тАУ13), which in this reprise is depicted as far more of an even match. Vr╠еtra strikes at Indra with his fangs and deploys various natural forces against his adver sary. This more equal battle is encapsulated in the perfectly balanced construction ├нndra┼Ы ca ya╠Бd yuyudh─Б╠Бte a╠Бhi┼Ы ca тАЬwhen Indra and the serpent fought each other… тАЭ (13c). It is unclear why the first triumphalist account has been revised to the more ambiguous, less glorious versionтАФthough both, of course, end with Vr╠еtraтАЩs defeat.
The most mysterious part of this hymn is the conclusion. Vr╠еtra is dead, and even his mother D─Бnu has been killed, so there is no possibility of a new Vr╠еtra. And yet Indra apparently becomes terrified and flies across the rivers тАЬlike a frightened falcon.тАЭ Perhaps this puzzling ending is related to the second version of the battle, in which Indra does not have quite the unchallenged heroic role that he plays in the first version. The poet does not explain but in the last verse simply returns to a praise of Indra as victor and king.

English translation:

тАЬI declare the former valorous deeds of Indra, which the thunderer has achieved; he clove the cloud; he cast the waters down (to earth); he broke (a way) for the torrents of the mountain.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vс╣Ыtra, also called Ahi, is alluded to as condensed accusative ulation of vapour figuratively shut up or obstructed by a cloud; Indra, with his thunderbolt or atmospheric prowess divides up the augmented mass yielding a vent for the rain to descend on the earth and moisten the fields

Jamison Brereton

Now I shall proclaim the heroic deeds of Indra, those foremost deeds that the mace-wielder performed:
He smashed the serpent. He bored out the waters. He split the bellies of the mountains.

Griffith

I WILL declare the manly deeds of Indra, the first that he achieved, the Thunder-wielder.
He slew the Dragon, then disclosed the waters, and cleft the channels of the mountain torrents.

Macdonell

I will proclaim the manly deeds of Indra, The first that he performed, the lightning-wielder. He slew the serpent, then discharged the waters, And cleft the caverns of the lofty mountains.

Grassmann

рд╡реГрд╖рд╛рдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ рд╡реГрд╖ рдЗрд╡рд╛рдЪрд░рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕реЛрдордореН рдЕрд╡реГрдгреАрдд рд╡реГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рддреНрд░рд┐рдХрджреНрд░реБрдХреЗрд╖реБ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдГ рдЧреМрдГ рдЖрдпреБрдГ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХрд╛рдГ рддреНрд░рдпреЛ рдпрд╛рдЧрд╛рдГ рддреНрд░рд┐рдХрджреНрд░реБрдХрд╛рдГ рдЙрдЪреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред рддреЗрд╖реБ рд╕реБрддрд╕реНрдп рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реЛрдорд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВрд╢рдореН рдЕрдкрд┐рдмрддреН рдкреАрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рдордШрд╡рд╛ рдзрдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрдВ рдмрдиреНрдзрдХрдВ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдореН рдЖ рдЕрджрддреНрдд рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХреГрддрд╡рд╛рдиреН ред рддреЗрди рдЪ рд╡рдЬреНрд░реЗрдг рдЕрд╣реАрдирд╛рдВ рдореЗрдШрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердордЬрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдердореЛрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирдВ рдореЗрдШрдореН рдЕрд╣рдиреН рд╣рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рее рд╡реГрд╖рд╛рдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ ред рд╡реГрд╖ рдЗрд╡рд╛рдЪрд░рдиреН ред тАШ рдХрд░реНрддреБрдГ рдХреНрдпрдЩреН рд╕рд▓реЛрдкрд╢реНрдЪ’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рей. рез. резрез ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреНрдпрдЩреНред тАШ рдЕрдХреГрддреНрд╕рд╛рд░реНрд╡рдзрд╛рддреБрдХрдпреЛрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГ ред рдЕрджреБрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН рдзрд╛рддреЛрдГ рдЕрдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡реЗ рдХреНрдпрдЩрдиреНрддрд╛рддреН рдзрд╛рддреЛрдГ рдЕрдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН (?)ред рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрдореН ред’ рд╖рд┐рдЮреН рдмрдиреНрдзрдиреЗ ред рд╕рд┐рдиреЛрддреАрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрдГ ред рдгреНрд╡реБрд▓реНред рд▓рд┐рддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд░реЗрдгрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдкреНрд░рдердордЬрд╛рдореН ред рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рдЬрд╛рдпрддреЗ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдердордЬрд╛рдГ ред тАШ рдЬрдирд╕рдирдЦрдирдХреНрд░рдордЧрдореЛ рд╡рд┐рдЯреН’ред рд╡рд┐рдбреНрд╡рдиреЛрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЖрддреНрд╡рдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬImpetuous as a bull, he quaffed the Soma juice, he drank of the libation at the triple sacrifice. Maghvan took his shaft, the thunderbolt, and with it struck the first born of the clouds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Triple sacrifice: at the trikadrukas, three sacrifices termed jyotiс╣г, gauс╕е and ─Бyu

Jamison Brereton

Acting the bull, he chose for his own the soma. He drank of the pressed soma among the Trikadrukas [=the Maruts?].
The generous one took up his missile, the mace. He smashed him, the first-born of serpents.

Griffith

Impetuous as a bull, he chose the Soma and in three sacred beakers drank the juices.
Maghavan grasped the thunder for his weapon, and smote to death this firstborn of the dragons.

Macdonell

Impetuous like a bull he chose the Soma, And drank in threefold vessels of its juices. The bounteous god grasped lightning for his missile; He struck down dead that first-born of the serpents.

Geldner

Grassmann

Als br├╝nst’ger Stier ersah er sich den Soma, aus den drei Eimern trank er den gebrauten, Als Waffe nahm den Blitz der allgewalt’ge, und t├╢dtete der Drachen erstgebornen.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╡рд╣ рдХреИрд╕рд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рд╡реГрд╖рд╛рдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ) рд╡реАрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд╛ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд▓реЛрдХ рдореЗрдШ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рд╕реБрддрд╕реНрдп) рдЗрд╕ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рд╣реБрдП рдЬрдЧрддреН рдХреЗ (рддреНрд░рд┐рдХрджреНрд░реБрдХреЗрд╖реБ) рдЬрд┐рдирдХреА рдЙрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐ рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░рддрд╛ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢ рдпреЗ рддреАрди рдХрд▓рд╛ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╣реИрдВ рдЙрди рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рд╕реЛрдордореН) рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рд╣реБрдП рд░рд╕ рдХреЛ (рдЕрд╡реГрдгреАрдд) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛ (рдЕрдкрд┐рдмрддреН) рдЙрд╕рдХреЛ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рддрд╛рдк рдореЗрдВ рднрд░ рд▓реЗрддрд╛ рдФрд░ (рдордШрд╡рд╛) рдпрд╣ рдмрд╣реБрдд рд╕рд╛ рдзрди рджрд┐рд▓рд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп (рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрдореН) рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд░реВрдк (рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдореН) рдХрд┐рд░рдг рд╕рдореВрд╣ рдХреЛ (рдЖрджрддреНрдд) рд▓реЗрддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдЕрд╣реАрдирд╛рдореН) рдореЗрдШреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдкреНрд░рдердордЬрд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рдердо рдкреНрд░рдЧрдЯ рд╣реБрдП (рдПрдирдореН) рдЗрд╕ рдореЗрдШ рдХреЛ (рдЕрд╣рдиреН) рдорд╛рд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИред рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рдЧреБрдг, рдХрд░реНрдо, рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддрд┐ рдХрд╛ рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░ рдкрд╛рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордВрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдмреИрд▓ рд╡реАрд░реНрдп рдХреЛ рдмрдврд╝рд╛ рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддрд┐ рджреВрдз рдЖрджрд┐ рдкреАрдХрд░ рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛ рдХреЗ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд╣реЛрд╡реЗ рдФрд░ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп рд░рд╕ рдХреЛ рдкреА рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╡рд░рд╕рд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рд╡реИрд╕реИ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЗ рдмрд▓ рдХреЛрдВ рдЦреАрдВрдЪ рдЕрдкрдирд╛ рдмрд▓ рдмрдврд╝рд╛ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреА рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХрд░реЗ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

(рд╡реГрд╖рд╛рдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ) рд╡реГрд╖ рдЗрд╡рд╛рдЪрд░рдиреН (рдЕрд╡реГрдгреАрдд) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд▓рдбрд░реНрдереЗ рд▓рдЩ (рд╕реЛрдордореН) рд╕реВрдпрдд рдЙрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрддрдВ рд░рд╕рдореНред (рддреНрд░рд┐рдХрджреНрд░реБ рдХреЗрд╖реБ) рддреНрд░рдп рдЙрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд▓рдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдХрджреНрд░рд╡реЛрд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдзрдХрд▓рд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗрд╖реБ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрд╖реБред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдХрджрд┐рдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реМрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГ рдХреНрд░реБрдиреНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГред рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕рдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдХрдкреН рдЪред (рдЕрдкрд┐рдмрддреН) рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрди рдкрд┐рдмрддрд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд▓рдбрд░реНрдереЗ рд▓рдЩреН (рд╕реБрддрд╕реНрдп) рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирд╕реНрдп рдЬрдЧрддреЛ рдордзреНрдпреЗ (рдЖ) рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдпреЛрдЧреЗред (рд╕рд╛рдпрдХрдореН) рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдореН (рдордШрд╡рд╛) рдордШрдВ рдмрд╣реБрд╡рд┐рдзрдВ рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрдВ рдзрдирдВ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГред рдЕрддреНрд░ рднреВрдореНрдиреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рдорддреБрдкреНред (рдЕрджрддреНрддреН) рджрджрд╛рддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд▓рдЩреНред (рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдореН) рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╕рдореВрд╣рдорд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдореН (рдЕрд╣рдиреН) рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд▓рдЩреНред (рдПрдирдореН) рдореЗрдШрдореН (рдкреНрд░рдердордЬрд╛рдо) рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рдЬрд╛рдпрддреЗ рддрдореНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдЬрдирд╕рдирежред рдЕреж рейредреиредремренред рдЕрдиреЗрди рдЬрдирдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдЯреН рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГред (рдЕрд╣реАрдирд╛рдореН) рдореЗрдШрд╛рдирд╛рдореН реерейрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch, Indra, as you have divided the first-born of the clouds, you have destroyed the delusions of the deluders, and then engendering the sun, the dawn, the firmament, you have not left an enemy (to oppose you).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

First-born of the clouds: the first-formed cloud

Jamison Brereton

When you, Indra, smashed the first-born of serpents and then beguiled the wiles of the wily ones,
then, giving birth to the sun, the heaven, and the dawn, since that time you have surely never found a rival.

Griffith

When, Indra, thou hadst slain the dragon’s firstborn, and overcome the charms of the enchanters,
Then, giving life to Sun and Dawn and Heaven, thou foundest not one foe to stand against thee.

Macdonell

When thou hadst slain the first-born of the serpents, And thwarted all the wiles of crafty schemers, Anon disclosing sun, and dawn, and heaven, Thou truly foundest not a foe, O Indra.

Geldner

Als du, Indra, den Erstgeborenen der Drachen erschlugst und da die Listen der Listigen noch ├╝berlistetest, da du Sonne, Himmel, Morgenr├╢te zum Vorschein brachtest, da hast du fortab nimmer deinen Meister gefunden.

Grassmann

Als, Indra, du der Drachen erstgebornen erschlugst, da tilgtest du der List’gen Listen, Und Sonne, Tag und Morgenr├╢the zeugend hast keinen Feind du damals mehr gefunden.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWith his vast destroying thunderbolt, Indra struck the darkling mutilated Vс╣Ыtra; as the trunks of trees are felled by the axe, so lies Ahi prostrate on the earth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ahi and Vс╣Ыtra are synonyms of megha, a cloud

Jamison Brereton

Indra smashed Vr╠еtra [/Obstacle] the very great obstacle, whose
shoulders were spread apart, with his mace, his great weapon.
Like logs hewn apart by an axe, the serpent would lie, embracing the earth [/soaking the earth (with his blood)].

Griffith

Indra with his own great and deadly thunder smote into pieces Vrtra, worst of Vrtras.
As trunks of trees, what time the axe hath felled them, low on the earth so lies the prostrate Dragon.

Indra slew Vс╣Ыtra and one worse than Vс╣Ыtra, Vyaс╣Гsa, with lightning, his resistless weapon: Like trunks of trees, with axes hewn in pieces, The serpent clinging to the earth lay prostrate.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe arrogant Vс╣Ыtra, as if unequaled, defied Indra, the mighty hero, the destroyer of many, the scatterer of foes; he has not escaped the contact of the fate (Indra’s) enemies. The foe of Indra has crushed the (banks of the) rivers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ruj─Бn─Бс╕е pipiс╣гe, he has ground the rivers or broken down the banks of the rivers, signifying the fall of Vс╣Ыtra

Jamison Brereton

For, like a drunken non-warrior, he challenged the hard-pressing great hero whose is the silvery drink [=soma].
(Vr╠еtra) did not withstand the attack of his weapons. His mouth
destroyed by the shattering blow, he whose rival was Indra was
completely crushed.

Griffith

He, like a mad weak warrior, challenged Indra, the great impetuous many-slaying Hero.
He, brooking not the clashing of the weapons, crushed–Indra’s foe–the shattered forts in falling.

Macdonell

He like a drunken coward challenged Indra, The headlong, many-crushing, mighty hero. He parried not the onset of the weapons: The foe of Indra, falling, crushed the channels.

Geldner

Denn er hatte wie ein des K├дmpfens Unkundiger in trunkenem ├Ьbermut den gro├Яen Helden, den Starkbedr├дngenden, Trestersomatrinkenden herausgefordert. Er hat den Anprall seiner Waffen nicht ausgehalten; der Nasenbrecher wurde zerschmettert, als er in Indra seinen Meister fand.

Grassmann

Denn wie ein trunkner Feigling hatt’ den Helden den tilgenden, gewalt’gen er gefordert, Er hielt nicht aus den Andrang seiner Hiebe, im Sturz zerbrach der Indrafeind die Kl├╝fte.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬHaving neither hand nor foot, he defied Indra, who struck him with the thunderbolt upon his mountain-like shoulder, like one emasculated who pretends to virility; then Vс╣Ыtra, mutilated of many members, slept.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Handless and footless, he gave battle to Indra. (Indra) smashed his mace upon his back.
A steer who tried to be the measure of a bull, Vr╠еtra lay there, flung
apart in many places.

Griffith

Footless and handless still he challenged Indra, who smote him with his bolt between the shoulders.
Emasculate yet claiming manly vigour, thus Vrtra lay with scattered limbs dissevered.

Macdonell

Footless and handless he with Indra battled, Who smote him then upon his back with lightning. But, impotent, he strove to match the hero: He lay with scattered limbs in many places.

Fusslos und handlos stritt er wider Indra; der schleuderte den Blitz auf seinen R├╝cken, Der mit dem Stier sich messen wollt’, der H├дmmling, Vritra lag da zerst├╝ckt an vielen Orten.

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддреМ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реБрдд рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗред

English translation:

тАЬThe mother of Vс╣Ыtra was bending over her son, when Indra struck her nether part with his shaft; so the mother was above and the son underneath, and D─Бnu slept (with her son), like a cow with its calf.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

D─Бnu derived from do, to cut or destroy or from D─Бnu wife of K─Б┼Ыyapa and mother of the D─Бnavas or Titans

Jamison Brereton

The strength of Vr╠еtraтАЩs mother ebbed; Indra bore his weapon down upon her.
The mother was above; the son below: D─Бnu lies like a milk-cow with her calf.

The mother was above, the son was under and like a cow beside her calf lay Danu.

Geldner

Zur Neige ging die Lebenskraft der Mutter des Vritra; Indra hatte die Waffe auf sie geschleudert. Obenauf lag die Erzeugerin, zuunterst der Sohn. Die Danu liegt wie die Kuh bei ihrem Kalbe.

Grassmann

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдп рд╢рд░реАрд░рдВ рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рдХреНрд╡ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреАрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

English translation:

тАЬWhen the single resplendent Vс╣Ыtra returned the blow (which had been inflicted), Indra, by your thunderbolt, you became (furious), like a horse’s tail. You have rescued the kine; you have won, Hero, the Soma juice; you have let loose the seven rivers to flow.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like a horse’s tail, as a horse lashes his tail to get rid of the flies; seven rivers: gaс╣Еg─Б, yamun─Б, sarasvat─л, ┼Ыatudr─л, paruс╣гс╣З─л (ir─Бvat─л), asikni, marudvс╣Ыdh─Б, vitast─Б, ─Бrj─лk─лya (vip─Бs─Б) and suс╣гom─Б (sindhu)

Jamison Brereton

You, Indra, then became the tail of a horse when he struck his fangs at youтАФyou, the god alone.
You conquered the cows, and, o champion, you conquered the soma. You set loose the seven rivers to flow.

Griffith

A horse’s tail wast thou when he, O Indra, smote on thy bolt; thou, God without a second,
Thou hast won back the kine, hast won the Soma; thou hast let loose to flow the Seven Rivers.

Macdonell

A horse’s tail thou didst become, O Indra, When, on his spear impaled, as god unaided, The cows, O hero, thou didst win and Soma, And free the seven streams to flow in torrents.

Geldner

In ein Ro├Яhaar verwandeltest du dich da, Indra, als er dich gegen die Zacke schlug. Der einzige Gott erobertest du die K├╝he, du erobertest, o Held, den Soma; du lie├Яest die sieben Str├╢me frei, da├Я sie laufen.

Grassmann

Du warst ein Rossschweif, Indra, als er damals im Schuss dich traf; du, der allein du Gott bist, Gewannst die K├╝he, Held, gewannst den Soma, und rinnen liessest du die sieben Str├╢me.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬNeither the lightning nor the thunder (discharged by Vс╣Ыtra), nor the rain which he showered, nor the thunderbolt, harmed Indra, when he and Ahi contended and Maghvat triumphed also over other (attacks).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Neither the lightning nor the thunder, neither the mist nor the hail that he scattered repelled (Indra) for him.
When Indra and the serpent fought each other, the generous one
achieved victory also for (all) later times.

Griffith

Nothing availed him lightning, nothing thunder, hailstorm or mist which had spread around him:
When Indra and the Dragon strove in battle, Maghavan gained the victory for ever.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen fear entered, Indra, into your heart when about to slay Ahi, what other destroyer of him did you look for, that, alarmed, you did traverse ninety and nine streams like a (swift) hawk?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

When fear entered Indra: his fear was the uncertainty whether he should destroy Vс╣Ыtra or not

Jamison Brereton

Whom did you see, Indra, as the avenger of the serpent when fear came into your heart after you smashed him,
and when you crossed over the ninety-nine flowing rivers, like a
frightened falcon through the airy realms?

Griffith

Whom sawest thou to avenge the Dragon, Indra, that fear possessed thy heart when thou hadst slain him;
That, like a hawk affrighted through the regions, thou crossedst nine-and-ninety flowing rivers?

Macdonell

Whom saw’st thou as avenger of the serpent, As terror seized thy heart when thou hadst slain him, And thou didst cross the nine and ninety rivers And air’s broad spaces, like a hawk affrighted?

Geldner

Wen sahst du, Indra, als R├дcher des Drachen, da├Я Furcht dein, des T├╢ters, Herz befiel, als du ├╝ber die neunundneunzig Str├╢me, wie der Adler erschreckt die R├дume durcheiltest?

Grassmann

Wen sahst du, Indra, als des Drachens R├дcher, als dir dem Sieger damals Furcht ins Herz schlich, Als du die Flut der neunundneunzig Str├╢me, die Luft durchflogst wie ein erschreckter Falke?

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдпреЛрдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдХрд┐рдВ рднрд╡рддреАрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗред

(рдЕрд╣реЗрдГ) рдореЗрдШрд╕реНрдп (рдпрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдореН) рджреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдореН (рдХрдореН) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрдиреНрдпрдореН (рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдпрдГ) рдкрд╢реНрдпреЗрддреНред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд▓рд┐рдЩрд░реНрдереЗ рд▓рдЩреНред (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╢рддреНрд░реБрджрд▓рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдХ рдпреЛрджреНрдзрдГ (рд╣реГрджрд┐) рд╣реГрджрдпреЗ (рдпрддреН) рдзрдирдореН (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдЬрдШреНрдиреБрд╖рдГ) рд╣рдиреНрддреБрдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН (рднреАрдГ) рднрдпрдореН (рдЕрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреН) рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд▓рдЩреНред (рдирд╡) рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ (рдЪ) рдкреБрдирд░рд░реНрдереЗ (рд╕реНрд░рд╡рдиреНрддреАрдГ) рдЧрдордирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреАрд░реНрдирджреАрд░реНрдирд╛рдбрд╝реАрд░реНрд╡рд╛ред рд╕реНрд░рд╡рдиреНрддреНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рдирджреАрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореНред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж резредрезрейред рд╕реНрд░реБрдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реНрдЧрддреНрдпрд░реНрдерддреНрд╡рд╛рджреНрд░реБрдзрд┐рд░рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдЧрдордирдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛ рдЬреАрд╡рдирд╣реЗрддрд╡реЛ рдирд╛рдбреНрдпреЛрдкрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗред (рд╢реНрдпреЗрдирдГ) рдкрдХреНрд╖реА (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рднреАрддрдГ) рднрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдГ (рдЕрддрд░рдГ) рддрд░рддрд┐ (рд░рдЬрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд▓реНрдБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдиреН рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рд░рдЬрд╛рдВрд╕реНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрдВрддреЗред рдирд┐рд░реБреж рекредрезрепред реерезрекрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThen Indra, the wilder of the thunderbolt, became the sovereign of all that is moveable or immoveable, of hornless and horned cattle; and as he abides the monarch of men, he comprehended all things (within him), as the circumference comprehends the spokes of a wheel.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Bearing the mace in his arms, Indra is the king of him who travels and of him who is settled, of the horned and the hornless.
And just he alone as king rules over the different peoples: like a rim the spokes of a wheel, he encompasses those.

Griffith

Indra is King of all that moves and moves not, of creatures tame and horned, the Thunder-wielder.
Over all living men he rules as Sovran, containing all as spokes within the felly.

Macdonell

Indra is king of all that’s fixed and moving, Of tame and horned beasts, the thunder-wielder. He truly rules, as king of busy mortals; Them he encompasses as spokes the felly.

Grassmann

Was geht und steht, beherrscht als K├╢nig Indra, das arbeitsame Vieh und das geh├╢rnte, Den Blitz im Arm beherrscht er alle Menschen, umfasst sie wie des Rades Kranz die Speichen.

Elizarenkova
